**2026-05-14 14:00:00Z** - **FIX**: post-edc11aa review followups. Two findings: **#1 Medium (delegated_pull logs failures as ok).** `service/core.rs:291` used `ok = !cancelled`, but `handle_delegated_pull` returned `()` and converted `run_delegated_pull` failures into an error-progress message on `tx`. So a real handler failure with the client still connected logged `delegated_pull ok ... errors=N` with `N` unchanged — the operator-facing metric contradicted the actual RPC result. Fix: `handle_delegated_pull` now returns `bool` (true=success, false=failure). The phased error is still surfaced on `tx` as before; the bool is purely the success bit. Caller in `service/core.rs` consumes via `tokio::select!` into `Option<bool>` — `None` = client cancelled, `Some(true)` = handler ok, `Some(false)` = handler failed. `ok = matches!(outcome, Some(true))`; `inc_error` fires only on `Some(false)` (handler failure), not on client cancellation. New regression test `handle_delegated_pull_returns_false_on_handler_failure` drives a blank-host source locator to trip `DelegationRejected` and asserts `false` is returned — pins the return-bool contract without mocking the full pipeline. **#2 Low (release-plan inconsistency).** Top-tracker said §3.1/§3.2/§3.3 closed, but §6 commit-sequence table still labeled steps 9–11 "Not started," step 1 said D4/D5/D6 still open, step 13 still claimed tagging is blocked on "product-owner ack of P1 deferrals," and §7 heading still said D4/D5/D6 are open. All four sites rewritten to reflect 2026-05-13 reality: steps 9–11 carry closing commits (`0d76c4f`, `6e750b9`, `6e750b9`); step 1 says "all taken — D5 modified by owner"; step 13 shows tagging blocked on step 2 only; §7 heading says "all D1–D9 decided, nothing owed anymore" with the section name retained for historical reference. **Tests**: `cargo fmt --all -- --check` clean; `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean; `cargo test --workspace` all pass (+1 delegated_pull regression test).

**2026-05-14 12:00:00Z** - **FIX**: post-6e750b9 review followups against the --metrics work. Four findings: **#1 Medium (active-gauge race).** `format_completion_line` was reading `active_transfers` while the just-finished RPC's `_guard` was still in scope, so a single completed transfer logged `active=1` — misleading for an end-of-RPC summary. Fix: rename `let _guard = guard;` to `let guard = guard;` and `drop(guard);` explicitly before the `log_completion` call in all three spawn closures (push / pull / pull_sync at `service/core.rs`). Now `active=N` reflects state AFTER the just-finished RPC is removed from the gauge. **#2 Medium (missing RPC coverage).** `delegated_pull` increments `pull_ops` + the active gauge inside `run_delegated_pull` (`delegated_pull.rs:227`) but never emitted its own completion line — the field would only become visible on a later push/pull log. Same for `purge`. Fix: (a) wrapped the delegated_pull spawn closure in core.rs with a start-time capture and a `log_completion("delegated_pull", ...)` call after the cancellation `select!`; `ok = !cancelled` per the cancellation-race semantics. (b) Extracted `BlitService::purge_inner` so the trait `purge` method can wrap a single call site with start-time capture + `log_completion("purge", ...)` + `inc_error` on `Err`. Both paths now contribute to `--metrics` per-RPC summary symmetrically. **#3 Medium (rustfmt clean).** Already clean on `HEAD` (the prior `cargo fmt --all` at the tail of `6e750b9` had landed); reviewer was working off an older snapshot. No action. **#4 Low (stale scope text).** Three sites still claimed `--metrics` was dormant / scaffolding-only after the §3.1 closure: (a) `crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:82` comment block rewritten to reference `log_completion` and call out the new operator-facing summary lines; the `--metrics` `eprintln!` info line now says "per-RPC summary lines on stderr." (b) `docs/plan/RELEASE_PLAN_v2_2026-05-04.md:500` — old "No reader / dormant" analysis paragraph quoted as historical context inside a "Resolved 2026-05-13" callout, so the section reads consistently as closed without losing the audit-time reasoning. (c) `TODO.md:248` — AI telemetry line struck through with explicit `Removed from scope 2026-05-13` callout pointing at §5.4 + deletion of the doc; predictor note added to clarify perf-history collection is unaffected. **New regression test:** `completion_line_reflects_active_after_guard_drop` constructs an in-flight transfer + a finishing transfer, drops the finishing guard, and asserts `active=1` in the formatted line — pins the call-site contract that the formatter sees post-drop state. **Verified:** `cargo fmt --all -- --check` clean, `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean, `cargo test --workspace` all pass (+1 new metrics test, 9 total in `metrics::tests`).

**2026-05-13 18:30:00Z** - **FEAT + SCOPE**: §3.1 / §3.3 / §5.2 / §5.4 closed (D5 modified, D6 default taken, BlitAuth + AI telemetry removed). Three owner decisions landed in one commit set: **(1) §3.1 D5 modified.** Rather than ship `--metrics` as dormant scaffolding, the daemon now emits a one-line stderr summary at end of each push/pull/pull_sync RPC when `--metrics` is on. Format: `[metrics] push ok in 1.23s (push_ops=N pull_ops=N purge_ops=N active=N errors=N)` — rsync/rclone-style operator visibility under systemd / foreground without needing the TUI. `crates/blit-daemon/src/metrics.rs` gains `log_completion(op_kind, duration, ok)` (no-op when disabled — atomics never loaded) and `format_completion_line` (extracted so the format contract is unit-testable without stderr capture). 3 new unit tests in `metrics::tests` pin the line format and error tagging. **2026-05-05 20:30:00Z** - **FIX**: Round 45 review of commit `f83a208`. **R45-F1 (High)**: while plumbing scanned features I left a `let total_bytes = scanned_bytes` alias in `crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/orchestrator.rs:480` and the streaming summary at `:567` then read that local for `summary.total_bytes`. Net effect on the wire: `summary.total_bytes` (contracted as "bytes the pipeline wrote") was reporting scanned bytes, so any incremental skip-unchanged run with all-up-to-date files would have reported the full source size as bytes-written and overcounted throughput. Fix: removed the alias; streaming summary now reads `pipeline_outcome.bytes_written` from `SinkOutcome` directly. The verbose "Planning enumerated" line correctly references `scanned_bytes`. **R45-F2 (Low)**: planner + transfer sub-predictions were still passing `(all_headers.len(), total_bytes)` (which were aliases of scanned_* but only by accident) while the total prediction passed `(scanned_files, scanned_bytes)` explicitly. Made all three predictor calls share the explicit `(scanned_files, scanned_bytes)` feature vector so a future maintainer editing one branch can't reintroduce drift by missing another. New regression test `incremental_run_total_bytes_excludes_skipped_files` in `orchestrator::orchestrator::async_runtime_tests` runs the full local mirror pipeline twice (mirror=true forces streaming planner; skip_unchanged=true means run 2 writes 0 bytes) and asserts `summary.total_bytes == 0` on the second run. Verified the test catches the bug by reintroducing the alias — assertion fires with `total_bytes=4096, scanned_bytes=4096` matching the pre-R45 state. **Tests**: `cargo test --workspace` 407 pass / 0 fail (was 406, +1 new R45 regression test).

**2026-05-05 19:30:00Z** - **FIX**: Round 44 review of commit `da6ced2`. **R44-F1 (Medium)**: predictor train/query feature mismatch. The pre-pipeline query in `crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/orchestrator.rs` used `(all_headers.len(), total_bytes)` (scan-side workload), but `record_performance_history` recorded `summary.copied_files` for `PerformanceRecord.file_count`. On any incremental run the predictor saw "predict 1000 files" then trained on "5 files actually copied" — estimates drifted badly. Fix: added `scanned_files: usize` and `scanned_bytes: u64` to `LocalMirrorSummary` (`crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/summary.rs`) with a load-bearing rustdoc explaining the scan-vs-copy split; populated at every summary construction site (streaming pipeline, NoWork, Tiny, Huge, JournalSkip, single-file copy); `record_performance_history` now reads `summary.scanned_{files,bytes}` for the record's feature fields. The bucket-shape counters (`tar_shard_*`, `raw_bundle_*`, `large_*`) still reflect actual writes — they feed `derive_local_plan_tuning` which heuristically sizes destination buckets from past apply behavior, not scan size. Extracted `build_performance_record` from `record_performance_history` so the contract is unit-testable without polluting the global JSONL. Two new tests in `orchestrator::history::tests`: `record_uses_scanned_features_not_copied` (would have failed pre-fix on a 1000-scanned/5-copied incremental) and `bucket_counts_still_reflect_actual_writes` (regression guard against accidentally rerouting bucket counters through scan stats). **R44-F2 (Low)**: `blit profile --json` shape was unasserted. The pre-fix commit message claimed top-level `"predictor": null` for the empty-state, but actual output emits `{"copy": null, "mirror": null}` (predictor file loads even when no profile yet has training data). Picked the structured shape — strictly more informative — and pinned it in `test_utils_profile_json` (`crates/blit-cli/tests/blit_utils.rs`) with assertions covering both empty and trained states. **R44 plan note**: §2.8 of `docs/plan/RELEASE_PLAN_v2_2026-05-04.md` is correctly framed now as "predictor observability and training," not "adaptive planning behavior" — the predictor is queried, surfaced via `--verbose` and `blit profile --json`, and audit-able, but the Tiny fast-path still does not consult it for routing. **2026-05-05 18:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: §2.8 phase 2 of `docs/plan/RELEASE_PLAN_v2_2026-05-04.md` — orchestrator and `blit profile` now actually query the predictor. Three load-bearing changes: (1) `crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/orchestrator.rs` introduces a `plan_done = Instant::now()` checkpoint between the planner stage and the pipeline so `planner_duration_ms` and `transfer_duration_ms` are correctly attributed; pre-fix both fields fed `record_performance_history` got the same whole-run time, so v1 predictor training collapsed into a single regressor. (2) Just before kicking off `execute_sink_pipeline`, the orchestrator queries `predictor.predict(DurationKind::Total/Planner/Transfer, ...)` with the just-scanned `all_headers.len()` and `total_bytes`; populates `LocalMirrorSummary.predictor_estimate` (new field of type `PredictorEstimate { planner_ms, transfer_ms, total_ms, observations, fallback_depth }` in `summary.rs`). `--verbose` now emits two lines: a "Predictor estimate: ..." pre-run line and a "Predictor delta: ..." post-run line showing predicted-vs-actual percent error per phase. (3) `crates/blit-cli/src/profile.rs::run_profile` now calls `predictor.coefficients_for(mode-only, ...)` for both Copy and Mirror, surfaces the result as a coefficients block in human output (`alpha_ms_per_file`, `beta_ms_per_mb`, `gamma_ms` per planner/transfer pair) and as a `predictor.{copy,mirror}` JSON object under `--json`. **2026-05-05 18:00:00Z** - **ACTION**: §2.8 phase 1 of `docs/plan/RELEASE_PLAN_v2_2026-05-04.md` — extended the predictor data model so its predictions can actually drive decisions. Schema bumped to v2; existing `PerformancePredictor::load` already drops state on version mismatch, so the bump is transparent. New types: `DurationCoefficients` (planner + transfer coefficient pair per profile), `DurationKind { Planner, Transfer, Total }`, `Prediction { predicted_ms, observations, fallback_depth }`. New API: `predict(kind, mode, src_fs, dst_fs, fast_path, skip_unchanged, checksum, file_count, total_bytes) -> Option<Prediction>` walks a fallback chain — exact key → drop fast_path → drop dest_fs → drop src_fs → mode-only — gated at each step by `MIN_OBSERVATIONS_FOR_CONFIDENCE = 5`. `predict_planner(record)` / `predict_transfer(record)` / `predict_total(record)` are convenience wrappers around `predict(...)`. `coefficients_for(...)` returns the same `DurationCoefficients` clone that `blit profile --json` will surface in phase 2. `observe(record)` now updates BOTH coefficient sets in lockstep (single shared observation counter) so `transfer_duration_ms` becomes a load-bearing input. Removed the old `predict_ms(record) -> f64` and `predict_planner_ms(...) -> Option<(f64, u64)>` — both pre-v2 entry points returned values without confidence gating. Eight new unit tests added: `predict_below_confidence_threshold_returns_none`, `predict_above_confidence_threshold_returns_value` (verifies `fallback_depth == 0`), `predictor_learns_planner_and_transfer_independently`, `predict_total_sums_planner_and_transfer`, `fallback_chain_drops_fast_path_then_dest_then_src`, `schema_version_mismatch_resets_state_on_load`. Existing tests rewritten to use the new API. Phase 2 (orchestrator wire + verbose surface + `blit profile --json` exposure + Tiny fast-path extension when planner-dominant) lands in the next commit. **Tests**: `cargo test --workspace` 404 pass / 0 fail (was 399, +5 new predictor tests + 3 retained-with-new-API).

**2026-05-05 17:00:00Z** - **FIX**: R43 follow-up to R42-F2. The R42 commit added a comment on `MultiStreamSender::finish` claiming it routed through `drain_pipeline_error`, but the body still hand-rolled the same match arms — comment lied about the factoring. Real fix: extracted `drain_pipeline_outcome(handle: JoinHandle<...>) -> Result<SinkOutcome>` as the underlying primitive (Ok-on-clean / wrap-on-err / panic-prefix-on-join). `drain_pipeline_error` now delegates to it for the failure cases and only adds the "Ok-but-channel-closed" race-diagnostic on top. `finish()` calls `drain_pipeline_outcome(handle).await?` directly. Added 3 new unit tests in `drain_pipeline_error_tests`: `drain_outcome_returns_value_on_clean_finish` (passes the SinkOutcome through), `drain_outcome_wraps_pipeline_error` (same "data plane pipeline failed" wrapping that `queue()` produces, regardless of which call site triggered it), `drain_outcome_surfaces_panic_message`. **Tests**: `cargo test --workspace` 399 pass / 0 fail (was 396, +3).

**2026-05-05 16:00:00Z** - **FIX**: §2.7 of `docs/plan/RELEASE_PLAN_v2_2026-05-04.md` — closed `docs/plan/POST_REVIEW_FIXES.md` Round 1. **§1.1**: `let _ = file.flush().await` in `sink.rs::write_file_stream` now propagates as a `Status::internal`-style error via `with_context("flushing {dst}")?` — flush failure is a data-loss signal (user believes file is durable when it isn't). Six other "best-effort metadata" sites in `sink.rs` (block-complete mtime/perms, tar-shard mtime/perms, file-payload mtime, write_block_complete mtime/perms) plus three TCP socket tuning sites in `data_plane.rs` (`set_keepalive`, `set_send_buffer_size`, `set_recv_buffer_size`) plus two `local_worker.rs::single_file_mmap_copy` mtime sites converted from silent `let _ = ...` to `if let Err(e) = ... { log::warn!(...) }` so misconfigurations are visible without making them hard transfer errors. **§1.1b**: `MultiStreamSender::queue` in `crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs` no longer turns "tx.send failed" into the generic `"data plane pipeline closed unexpectedly"` string. `pipeline_handle` is now `Option<JoinHandle<...>>`; on send-failure, `take()` it, await, and surface the underlying error (`Ok(Err(e))` → `e.wrap_err("data plane pipeline failed")`, `Err(join)` → panic message). New regression test `pipeline_streaming_surfaces_underlying_sink_error` in `pipeline.rs::tests` uses a `FailingSink` to assert the underlying error message reaches the caller verbatim. **§1.2**: `TarShardExecutor` decision — kept with a thorough docstring explaining (a) gRPC-fallback streaming framing differs from TCP path's contiguous-buffer apply, requiring a `TarShardReceiver` trait extraction to unify, and (b) buffer-pool sizing benefits from real fallback throughput numbers. Deferred to post-0.1.0; tracked in `POST_REVIEW_FIXES.md` §1.2. **§1.3**: `WHITEPAPER.md` §3 "Data plane wire format" updated — `BLOCK_COMPLETE := 0x03 path_len:u32 path:bytes total_size:u64 mtime:i64 perms:u32` (was missing the trailing `mtime + perms` shipped in `a7d659f`); added an explanatory paragraph on why the metadata trails the terminator. `POST_REVIEW_FIXES.md` Round 1 status block flipped to "Closed 2026-05-05". **Tests**: `cargo test --workspace` 393 pass / 0 fail (was 392, +1 new pipeline-streaming regression test).

**2026-05-02 22:15:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 15 finding R15-F1 (Low) — F11's user-facing closure. The previous F11 fix added daemon ack-mismatch handling in `RemotePullClient::pull_sync`, but `transfers/endpoints.rs::ensure_remote_transfer_supported` rejected `--checksum` for ALL remote transfers before the new code could fire. F11's CLI behavior was therefore unreachable. Made the gate direction-aware: `ensure_remote_pull_supported` allows `--checksum` (the F11 ack negotiates), `ensure_remote_push_supported` keeps it rejected for push/remote-remote (no equivalent capability negotiation in the push protocol yet). New integration test `remote_checksum_negotiation.rs` spins up a daemon with `--no-server-checksums`, runs `blit copy --checksum server:/test/file.txt dest`, and asserts (a) the client refuses with a clear ack-mismatch error, (b) no file is copied via silent fallback. Companion test confirms the same command succeeds against a daemon with checksums enabled. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (188 lib + 23 daemon + 27 metrics-test bin + 2 new checksum-negotiation integration tests, all green).

**2026-05-02 21:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed F5, F11, F12, F9 from `docs/reviews/codebase_review_2026-05-01.md` — the lower-priority items from the baseline triage. **F5** (Medium): replaced inc_active/dec_active scattered around `service/core.rs` with `TransferMetrics::enter_transfer() -> ActiveGuard`, an RAII handle that decrements on Drop so panics/cancellation can't leak the gauge. **2026-05-02 20:15:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 13 finding R13-F1 (Medium). The F2 fix protected per-file writes via `resolve_contained_path`, but the push-mirror purge path enumerates `module.path` (post-mutation by `destination_path`) before the per-entry containment check fires. If the supplied `destination_path` traversed an in-module symlink pointing outside the module root, the purge would enumerate outside the canonical root before refusing any individual delete. Two-layer fix: (1) `push/control.rs` now calls `verify_contained(&canonical_root, &new_path)` immediately after the destination_path mutation, rejecting the push at handshake; (2) `purge_extraneous_entries` calls `verify_contained` before enumeration, defense-in-depth for any future caller that bypasses the handshake check. New integration test `f2_push_destination_path_symlink_rejected` spins up a daemon, places `module/escape -> /sibling`, attempts `blit mirror src/ server:/test/escape/`, and asserts both the daemon refusal and that `/sibling`'s files were not touched. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (186 lib + 20 daemon + 3 F2 integration tests, all green).

**2026-05-02 19:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed F2 from `docs/reviews/codebase_review_2026-05-01.md` — the highest-severity remaining baseline finding. The lexical `safe_join` chokepoint catches `../`/abs/UNC/Windows-shaped wire paths but doesn't follow symlinks, so a pre-existing symlink inside a module pointing outside the root (e.g. `module/escape -> /etc`) would have any daemon read/write follow it. New `path_safety::contained_join` (and `verify_contained` for already-resolved targets) walks to the deepest existing ancestor, canonicalizes, and confirms `starts_with(canonical_module_root)`. 10 unit tests cover symlink-escape rejection (top-level, deep, parent-of-nonexistent), legit intra-module symlinks, lexical-traversal rejection, and the empty-rel single-file case. Wired into every daemon site that touches a path under a module root: `service/core.rs` (list, find, du, purge), `service/admin.rs` (delete_rel_paths_sync, stream_disk_usage, stream_find_entries), `service/pull.rs` and `service/pull_sync.rs` (pull entry-point), `service/push/data_plane.rs` (file dest + tar shard apply), `service/push/control.rs` (file_requires_upload). Added a separate `canonical_root: PathBuf` field on `ModuleConfig` because the push handler mutates `module.path` to bake in destination subpaths (rsync "copy into here" semantics) — containment must check against the never-mutated original. New integration tests in `crates/blit-cli/tests/f2_chroot_containment.rs` spin up a real daemon, place a symlink inside the module pointing outside, attempt to pull through it, assert the daemon refuses with a containment error, and verify the sensitive sibling file was not copied. Companion test confirms legit intra-module symlinks (`latest -> v1`) still work. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (186 lib + 20 daemon + integration suites, all green). F2 closes the last release-blocking security finding from the original baseline review.

**2026-05-02 18:00:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 11 finding R11-F1 (High) — completed F7 properly. The previous F7 fix bounded the *reservation* via `try_reserve_exact` but the actual `read_to_end` call would still grow the Vec past that bound if the remote source streamed extra bytes. A peer could declare `header.size = 4` and stream 1 GiB; the post-read length check would catch the discrepancy but only after the buffer had grown past the bound. Fix: extract `read_remote_entry_bounded` as a generic helper that wraps the reader with `tokio::io::AsyncReadExt::take(size + 1)` so the read itself is capped; the +1 is the over-read canary that triggers the post-read length check. Helper is `R: AsyncRead + Unpin` so tests use `std::io::Cursor` instead of a real `RemotePullClient` mock. 5 new tests in `remote_bounded_read_tests`: happy path, under-read, over-read (verifies buffer caps at size+1 even when source sends 1 MiB), defensive cap rejection, empty file. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (176 lib + 20 daemon + integration suites, all green). F7 now fully closed.

**2026-05-02 17:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed F7 + F8 from `docs/reviews/codebase_review_2026-05-01.md` (the original baseline review) in one small hardening pass. **F7** (now elevated to High in the triage): `RemoteTransferSource::prepare_payload` was doing `Vec::with_capacity(header.size as usize)` from a daemon-controlled `FileHeader.size` — the send-side mirror of R6-F1 that affects remote→remote transfers. Extracted `validate_remote_tar_shard_sizes` as a private helper that bounds both per-entry and cumulative shard sizes against `tar_safety::MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES`, uses `checked_add` for the sum, and is unit-testable without a `RemotePullClient` mock. Replaced the unbounded `Vec::with_capacity` with `try_reserve_exact`, plus an explicit length-match check after `read_to_end` so a remote source that lies about a file's size produces a hard error rather than a malformed tar. **F8**: `MAX_WIRE_TAR_SHARD_BYTES` in pipeline.rs was 1 GiB while the helper's `MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES` is 256 MiB — the wire reader accepted shards the helper would reject. Single source of truth: `MAX_WIRE_TAR_SHARD_BYTES = tar_safety::MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES as usize` (const). 5 new tests in `remote_tar_size_tests` (within bounds, at cap, per-entry above cap, cumulative above cap, u64 overflow). **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (171 lib + 20 daemon + integration suites, all green).

**2026-05-02 16:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 9 finding R9-F1 (Low). The R8-F2 fix (rejecting stream EOF without UploadComplete) was previously verified by code review only — the new framing-helper unit tests covered R8-F1 size/cap rules but not the actual EOF path through `receive_fallback_data`. To make the function unit-testable without a real gRPC server, generic-ified its signature over `tokio_stream::Stream<Item = Result<ClientPushRequest, Status>>` (tonic::Streaming already implements this trait, so production callers are unchanged) and switched the loop body from `.message()` to `.next().await.transpose()` — semantically identical. 3 new regression tests in `data_plane::tests` drive the function over `tokio_stream::iter` of synthetic message vectors: EOF after `FileManifest`, EOF after `TarShardHeader`, and EOF on an empty stream (no UploadComplete ever). All three assert the rejection now lives in the test suite, not just code review. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (166 lib + 20 daemon + integration suites, all green).

**2026-05-02 15:45:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 8 review findings R8-F1 and R8-F2 from `docs/reviews/followup_review_2026-05-02.md`. Both bugs were in the daemon's gRPC push fallback receive loop (`receive_fallback_data` in `crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs`) — the framing layer that runs *before* the shared `tar_safety` helper sees the buffer. **R8-F1** (Medium — DoS): the chunk accumulator was capped only by an 8 MiB initial reservation; the actual `Vec` grew unbounded. `archive_size == 0` skipped the overflow check entirely, and `archive_size > MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES` was bypassed at the framing layer. Reject zero archive_size when files are present, reject `archive_size > MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES` at TarShardHeader, and enforce both the declared size and the local cap on every chunk via a new `check_fallback_chunk_overflow` helper. **R8-F2** (Medium — silent partial success): stream EOF was treated as graceful end. But FileManifest and TarShardHeader remove entries from `pending` before bytes arrive, so a client could send a header, close the stream, and the final `pending.is_empty()` check would pass despite no data ever landing. Track `upload_complete_seen` and bail on EOF without UploadComplete or with `active.is_some()`. Extracted `validate_fallback_shard_archive_size` and `check_fallback_chunk_overflow` as private helpers so the rules are unit-testable without spinning up a full gRPC server. 7 new framing tests pin every boundary condition (zero size, at-cap, above cap, declared overflow, local-cap overflow, u64 overflow, within-bounds). **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (166 lib + 17 daemon + integration suites, all green).

**2026-05-02 14:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Round 7 cleanup — extracted shared `tar_safety` primitive in `blit-core/src/remote/transfer/tar_safety.rs` and migrated all three tar-shard receive sites onto it: `pull.rs::apply_pull_tar_shard` (gRPC fallback), `sink.rs::write_tar_shard_payload` (TCP data plane + local-local), `blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs::apply_tar_shard_sync` (daemon push receive). The migration closed a previously-latent High-severity bug on the daemon side: `apply_tar_shard_sync` was calling `Entry::unpack`, so an authenticated push client could ship a tar shard with a Symlink entry at a benign path pointing at `/etc/passwd` and a later push to that path would write through the symlink — same R5-F2 class as the pull side, but server-side. New regression test `apply_tar_shard_rejects_symlink_entry` proves the daemon now rejects non-regular entries up front. The shared helper also brought R6-F1 size bounds and R6-F3 mtime/permissions preservation to `sink.rs` and the daemon, where they were missing. 8 new unit tests in `tar_safety::tests`; net +8 lib tests workspace-wide (166 total). **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` all green.

**2026-05-02 13:15:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 6 review findings R6-F1 through R6-F3 from `docs/reviews/followup_review_2026-05-02.md`. **R6-F1** (Medium — DoS via per-entry size): `apply_pull_tar_shard` was preallocating with `Vec::with_capacity(header.size as usize)`, where `header.size` came from the daemon-authored `TarShardHeader.files`. A daemon could keep the shard `archive_size` under the 256 MiB cap while putting `u64::MAX` in a per-file header, forcing a huge initial allocation. Now validates `entry.size() == header.size` and `header.size <= shard.declared_size <= MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES` before any allocation, then uses `Vec::try_reserve_exact` so a still-pathological size returns `AllocError` instead of aborting. **R6-F2** (Medium — silent partial success): if the gRPC stream ended with `active_shard = Some(_)` (Header sent, no Complete), the receive loop dropped the buffered shard and returned success. Extracted the post-loop check into `ensure_no_open_shard` and made it bail with a wire protocol error — same treatment as `FileData` without a preceding `FileHeader`. **R6-F3** (Medium — metadata desync): manual tar-shard writes weren't applying `header.mtime_seconds` or `header.permissions`, so a forced-gRPC pull of many small files succeeded byte-for-byte but left destination mtimes at "now", causing the next size+mtime sync to re-transfer everything. Now applies mtime via `filetime::set_file_mtime` when `> 0` and Unix permissions when nonzero, mirroring `FsTransferSink`. 3 new unit tests in `tar_shard_safety_tests` (rejects oversized per-entry size, rejects open shard at end-of-stream, preserves mtime). **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (158 lib tests + integration suites, all green).

**2026-05-02 11:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 5 review findings R5-F1 through R5-F5 from `docs/reviews/followup_review_2026-05-02.md`. **R5-F1** (High — data-loss vector): `delete_listed_paths` used a lexical `target.starts_with(dest_root)` check that lets `dest_root.join("../victim")` pass. Routed every wire-supplied path through `path_safety::safe_join`, switched `RemotePullReport::paths_to_delete` from `Vec<PathBuf>` to `Vec<String>` so wire input never gets blessed into a path before validation, and added 4 unit tests in `delete_list_safety_tests` covering parent-traversal, absolute paths, root-self-reference, and the happy path. **R5-F2** (High — wire-controlled symlink/hardlink creation): `apply_pull_tar_shard` was calling `Entry::unpack` which honors tar's symlink/hardlink/device entry types. Rewrote to reject anything that isn't `EntryType::Regular` or `EntryType::Continuous`, validate the path through `validate_wire_path`, copy bytes manually, and verify per-entry size matches the corresponding `FileHeader.size`. Added 4 unit tests including a hand-crafted malicious tar with `../escape.txt` in its header. **R5-F3** (Medium — DoS via huge `archive_size`): `Vec::with_capacity(header.archive_size as usize)` was a daemon-controlled allocation. Added `MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES = 256 MiB` cap, modest initial reservation (capped at 1 MiB), per-chunk overflow check against `declared_size` and the local cap, and a final length check on `TarShardComplete`. **R5-F4** (Low — comment lied about validation): `filter_from_spec` claimed to validate glob patterns but only copied them into `FileFilter` for later silent dropping. Now compiles each include/exclude pattern through `globset::Glob::new` at the spec normalizer; 2 new tests pin rejection of malformed brackets. **R5-F5** (Low — DEVLOG ordering): added this header and moved newest entries to the top so review workflow doesn't depend on knowing how to find appended-at-the-bottom changes. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (152+ lib tests, all integration suites green).

**2026-05-02 09:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Step 4C — tar-shard support on the gRPC pull fallback. The push gRPC fallback runs the unified planner and emits TarShardHeader/Chunk/Complete for batched small-file workloads; the pull side previously sent files one-by-one via a hand-written loop. New `GrpcServerStreamingSink` (mirror of `GrpcFallbackSink`) in `blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs` lets the daemon's `stream_via_grpc` run `execute_sink_pipeline` with the same planner output as the TCP data plane. Proto adds three new ServerPullMessage variants (fields 13/14/15) reusing the existing TarShard message types. Client receive loop in `pull_sync` adds three match arms with an `InProgressShard` buffer and an `apply_pull_tar_shard` extractor (mirror of the daemon's push-side `apply_tar_shard_sync`). New integration test `test_pull_grpc_fallback_many_small_files` exercises 50 small files via `--force-grpc`. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (all green); `cargo test -p blit-cli --test remote_parity` (5 tests including the new one, all pass).

**2026-05-02 08:45:00Z** - **ACTION**: Step 4B — closed F10 (filter parity on pull) and F4 (mirror deletion correctness). The daemon now builds a `FileFilter` from `spec.filter` and threads it into `collect_pull_entries_with_checksums` so source enumeration honors `--exclude/--include/--min-size/--max-size/--min-age/--max-age/--files-from` exactly as a push would. After diff, a new `scope_deletions(...)` helper applies `MirrorMode` + filter scope and produces the authoritative deletion list, which the daemon ships to the client via a new `ServerPullMessage::DeleteList` variant. The CLI replaces the prior dest-tree-walking `purge_extraneous_local` with `delete_listed_paths`, which executes exactly what the daemon said (with bounded-path safety). New `--delete-scope <subset|all>` flag selects between `MirrorMode::FilteredSubset` (default — out-of-scope files preserved) and `MirrorMode::All` (every absent file purged). 6 new unit tests for scope_deletions; 2 new integration tests in `remote_pull_mirror` covering FilteredSubset preservation and `--delete-scope all` purge behavior. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (all green); `cargo test -p blit-cli --test remote_pull_mirror` (3 integration tests, all pass).

**2026-05-02 06:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed R2-F1, R4-F1, R4-F2, R4-F4 from `docs/reviews/followup_review_2026-05-02.md`. (1) DiffPlanner's `local_needs_copy` now has concrete behavior for every `ComparisonMode` (SizeOnly, IgnoreTimes, Force, Checksum, SizeMtime/Unspecified) instead of silently falling through to size+mtime; 10 new per-mode tests. (2) Daemon PullSync handler routes through `NormalizedTransferOperation::from_spec` so spec_version mismatch and unknown enum values become hard `invalid_argument` errors at the wire boundary. (3) `ignore_existing` is now an orthogonal `bool` field on `TransferOperationSpec` (proto field 10; old enum value 5 reserved); `compare_mode = Force && ignore_existing` is rejected at the spec normalizer; CLI adds `conflicts_with = "force"` on `--ignore-existing`; orchestrator threads the flag through `LocalMirrorOptions → LocalDiffInputs` so local-local copies enforce it through the same planner as remote paths. (4) Refreshed stale proto comments referring to removed `PullSyncHeader` and the old "supports_filter_spec fallback" plan. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (all green, 144+ core tests).

**2026-05-02 04:15:00Z** - **STEP 4A (PullSync wire migration to TransferOperationSpec)**: With no backwards-compat constraint into the next release, replaced the bool-soup `PullSyncHeader` (5 booleans for comparison mode + separate fields for resume/mirror/force_grpc) with the unified `TransferOperationSpec` defined in step 2. `ClientPullMessage::Header` is now `ClientPullMessage::Spec`. `PullSyncHeader` deleted from the proto entirely. Daemon parses the spec and translates its `ComparisonMode` enum onto the existing internal `CompareMode` via a new `compare_mode_to_internal` helper that also splits out `IgnoreExisting` as the orthogonal axis it actually is. Client (`RemotePullClient::pull_sync`) constructs the spec from CLI args, advertising full `PeerCapabilities` (resume, tar shards, data plane TCP, filter spec — all true), and defaulting `mirror_mode` to `MirrorMode::FilteredSubset` rather than the old "any-mirror-mode-true" boolean. Filter not yet honored on the daemon — that's step 4B. **The bool-soup → typed-enum win is real**: nonsensical combinations like `size_only=true && checksum=true && ignore_times=true` are no longer constructible. **Tests**: 214 pass (unchanged) — pure wire-shape migration, behavior preserved end-to-end.

**2026-05-02 03:30:00Z** - **STEP 3b (push client routes through diff_planner)**: Smaller than the orchestrator migration in step 3a because push's actual diff lives on the *daemon* side — the client sends its source manifest, the daemon returns a NeedList, and the client filters its headers to that intersection before planning. There's no client-side comparison stage to consolidate. What changed: added `plan_push_payloads(headers, source_root, plan_options)` to `diff_planner` as the unified entry point for push planning (a thin wrapper over `plan_transfer_payloads` that adds a `Context` for error messages); push client's import now goes through `diff_planner` so future readers find the planning entry point in the unified module rather than reaching into `payload.rs`. Documented inline that push's diff is daemon-driven and that step 5 (remote→remote re-evaluation) might let push share daemon-side diff machinery with pull. **Tests**: 214 pass (unchanged; this is a re-export + import rename, not a behavior change).

**2026-05-02 03:00:00Z** - **F1 follow-up (R1 fixes)**: Acted on `docs/reviews/followup_review_2026-05-02.md` round 1. **R1-F1** (Medium, real bug): `validate_wire_path` accepted single-leading-backslash forms like `\Windows\System32` on Unix because `Path::components` treats backslash as a normal character there. Extended `looks_like_windows_absolute` to flag any input starting with `\`. Tests added for `\foo`, `\foo\bar`, bare `\`. **R1-F3** (Low): wire path `"."` previously normalized to empty, getting the same single-file treatment as the legitimate empty-path case. `validate_wire_path` now rejects non-empty inputs that produce zero normal components (`"."`, `"./"`, `"./."`) — those are directory hints, not file paths. Fallout: the daemon's `resolve_relative_path` (used for list/find/du request paths where `.` legitimately means "module root") needed to disambiguate between request-path and file-path contexts. Added a request-path-context fold that maps `""`, `"."`, `"./"` etc. to `PathBuf::from(".")` before invoking strict validation; file-path callers (`resolve_manifest_relative_path`, sink writes) keep using the strict validator directly. **R1-F2** (Medium): `safe_join` is lexical only — `dest_root/symlink/file` lexically passes even when `symlink` escapes the root. Reviewer correctly identified this as F2 (chroot/canonical-containment) territory, not an F1 fix. Documented the lexical-only contract prominently in `path_safety.rs` module doc with an explicit pointer to F2 for canonical-parent containment. Updated `TODO.md` F2 entry to call out the symlink-traversal concern. **Tests**: 214 pass (was 213) — net +1 from R1-F1 leading-backslash test minus zero from R1-F3 (the existing `just_dot_normalizes_to_empty` test was rewritten as `just_dot_rejected` covering three inputs in one test).

**2026-05-02 02:30:00Z** - **STEP 3a (DiffPlanner extraction, orchestrator migration)**: New `blit-core::remote::transfer::diff_planner` module consolidates the diff + payload-planning stage. Public API: `plan_local_mirror(headers, LocalDiffInputs) -> PlannedPayloads` is the single entry point the orchestrator's local-mirror path now calls; under the hood it composes `filter_unchanged` (the comparison-filter stage previously named `filter_headers_for_copy` and inlined in `orchestrator.rs`) with the existing `plan_transfer_payloads`. Translates the proto `ComparisonMode` enum onto the `Option<ChecksumType>` that the existing comparison primitives consume — `Checksum` enables Blake3, all other variants (`Unspecified`, `SizeMtime`, `SizeOnly`, `IgnoreTimes`, `IgnoreExisting`, `Force`) currently fall back to size+mtime. The non-`SizeMtime` variants are accepted at the API surface so callers can pass them through; their proper behavior arrives with step 4 (pull_sync.rs migration brings the comparison strategies that today live as `PullSyncHeader` bools). Orchestrator's local-mirror path migrated: the previous inline scan → spawn_blocking(filter_headers_for_copy) → plan_transfer_payloads sequence is now scan → spawn_blocking(plan_local_mirror) — same effect, single chokepoint, smaller call site. Dead `filter_headers_for_copy` removed. `ChecksumType` gained `PartialEq + Eq` so the diff_planner unit tests can assert mappings. **Push and pull origin paths NOT yet migrated** — those land in step 3b and step 4 respectively. **Tests**: 213 pass (+4 new diff_planner unit tests covering the ComparisonMode→ChecksumType mapping for every variant, and the filter_unchanged identity-vs-modified behavior), 0 failures. Behavior preservation verified by the unchanged orchestrator integration tests (admin verbs, remote_remote, remote_pull_mirror, remote_resume, remote_tcp_fallback all still pass).

**2026-05-02 01:45:00Z** - **STEP 2 (operation spec contract)**: Added the canonical `TransferOperationSpec` message to `proto/blit.proto` along with `FilterSpec`, `ComparisonMode` enum, `MirrorMode` enum, `ResumeSettings`, `PeerCapabilities`. Per `docs/plan/PIPELINE_UNIFICATION.md` step 2: contract only, no behavior change yet. PushHeader and PullSyncHeader stay as the today-active control messages until the DiffPlanner extraction (step 3) and pull_sync.rs refactor (step 4) port to the new spec. Notable design choices: (1) `ComparisonMode` is an enum rather than the bool soup currently in PullSyncHeader (`size_only`, `ignore_times`, `ignore_existing`, `force`, `checksum` — five booleans that admit nonsensical combinations), (2) `MirrorMode` enum makes F4's filtered-mirror-delete-scope question explicit at the wire boundary (`OFF`, `FILTERED_SUBSET`, `ALL`), (3) `optional` proto3 scalars on `FilterSpec` size/age fields so callers can distinguish "not set" from "set to 0", (4) `PeerCapabilities` is additive — new capabilities default to `false` so a missing field on an old peer reads as "not supported." Re-export module `blit-core::remote::transfer::operation_spec` so callers don't reach into the generated `blit.v2` namespace directly. **Verification**: `cargo check --workspace` clean; `cargo test --workspace` 209 pass (unchanged); generated bindings include all six new types in the build artifact.

**2026-05-02 01:15:00Z** - **F1 (path safety)**: Centralized receive-side path validation in `blit-core/src/path_safety.rs`. Two helpers: `validate_wire_path(s) -> PathBuf` (pure validation, normalized form) and `safe_join(root, s) -> PathBuf` (validate + join, with empty input returning root unchanged for the single-file destination case). Rejects: `..` components (not just substrings — the previous tar-shard `rel.contains("..")` check was too weak and also rejected legitimate filenames containing literal `..`), absolute paths, Windows drive prefixes (`C:\…`), UNC and DOS device paths (`\\?\…`, `\\server\share\…`), root components, embedded NUL bytes. Migrated `pull.rs::sanitize_relative_path` and daemon `service/util.rs::resolve_relative_path` / `resolve_manifest_relative_path` to thin wrappers that delegate to the shared module — single chokepoint, no drift between sanitizers. Applied at all five receive-side sites the review identified: `sink.rs:218` (streamed file write), `sink.rs:404` + `:426` (tar shard entry validation + per-entry join), `sink.rs:462` (resume block write), `sink.rs:498` (block completion), and the gRPC fallback block-hash path in `pull.rs:532`. Wire-boundary defense in depth: `pipeline.rs::read_file_header` and per-entry path read in `read_tar_shard` validate at the moment paths arrive off the socket, so unsafe headers never enter the FileHeader stream. **Tests**: 209 passed (was 185 baseline) — 16 new `path_safety::tests` covering the validator surface (`..`, absolute Unix, Windows drive, UNC, NUL, valid `..`-containing filenames, deep paths, Unicode, trailing slash, just-dot), 8 new sink-level integration tests confirming `FsTransferSink::write_file_stream` rejects malicious wire paths before any filesystem write and that the legitimate single-file empty-path case still works. **Verification**: `cargo check --workspace` clean; `cargo test --workspace` 0 failures.

**2026-05-02 00:30:00Z** - **PLAN**: Architecture clarification in response to GPT-5.5's review of the universal-filter / blit check / daemon-metrics work and follow-up discussion. The review's findings (esp. F1 path safety, F10 filter parity overstatement, F11 pull checksum capability) revealed the deeper architectural shape: a transfer has three roles (initiator / origin / target) and `pull_sync.rs` is the only origin path that doesn't run the unified pipeline. The corrected model is documented in `docs/plan/PIPELINE_UNIFICATION.md`: the same pipeline (`TransferSource → DiffPlanner → execute_sink_pipeline_streaming → TransferSink`) runs on whichever side holds the data, regardless of where the CLI was invoked. The unified stage is `DiffPlanner`, not `FilteredSource` — `FilteredSource` is one input among filter rules, destination manifest, comparison mode, and capabilities. The wire contract is a normalized `TransferOperationSpec`, not a flag bag. Updated `TODO.md` with the 5-step priority sequence: F1 path safety first (independent prereq), then `TransferOperationSpec` data shape, then `DiffPlanner` extraction from `pull_sync.rs`, then `pull_sync.rs` refactor onto the unified pipeline, then re-evaluate remote→remote (currently CLI-mediated relay; should become daemon-A → daemon-B direct).

Highest-priority findings: receive-side path sanitization is incomplete across streamed files, tar shards, and resume block records; daemon `use_chroot` is documented/configured but not enforced; filtered mirror delete semantics need an explicit product decision; metrics lifecycle and endpoint behavior need hardening. Added a short `TODO.md` follow-up section and marked Phase 4 as in progress with the review artifact linked. **Verification**: `cargo check --workspace` passed; `cargo test --workspace` passed with 185 tests after rerunning outside the sandbox to allow local test port binding.

**2026-04-24 03:15:00Z** - **FIX**: Fixed single-file remote push crash — `blit copy FILE server:/mod/` previously died with "opening FILE/ during payload planning: Not a directory". Root cause was two-sided: on the client, `filter_readable_headers` and `build_tar_shard` computed `source_root.join(&rel)` where `rel=""` for single-file sources, which on Unix preserves a trailing `/` and makes `File::open` reject with ENOTDIR. On the daemon, `resolve_relative_path` folded empty paths to `"."` (which broke `module.path.join("")` = wanted single file, but got `module.path/.`), and the subsequent `module.path.join(empty_rel)` added another trailing `/`. Fix applies the `rel.is_empty() → use root directly` pattern in three places on the client side (matching `FsTransferSource::open_file`'s existing handling), and adds two new helpers on the daemon side: `resolve_manifest_relative_path` preserves empty as empty for per-file manifest entries, and `resolve_dest_path(base, rel)` handles the empty-rel join case. Swapped all four push-side `resolve_relative_path` callers and three `module.path.join` sites. Regression tests in `crates/blit-cli/tests/remote_push_single_file.rs` pin both the container-dir (`blit copy FILE server:/mod/`) and rename (`blit copy FILE server:/mod/new.txt`) cases. Annotated all four `docs/bugs/*.md` files with their resolution status. **Tests**: 173 passed (+2 remote push single-file), clippy clean.

**2025-01-29 10:00:00Z** - **FIX**: Addressed Gemini code review findings for remote block-level resume. (1) Fixed critical memory vulnerability: `compute_block_hashes` in `pull.rs` and both `stream_via_data_plane_resume`/`stream_via_block_resume_grpc` in `pull_sync.rs` now stream files in block-sized chunks instead of loading entire files into memory. (2) Fixed stop-and-wait protocol in data plane path: `stream_via_data_plane_resume` now pipelines all block hash requests upfront (Phase 1), collects all responses (Phase 2), then processes files (Phase 3) - eliminates per-file RTT penalty. gRPC fallback keeps simpler stop-and-wait since it's for diagnostic use only. **Tests**: `cargo build --package blit-daemon --package blit-cli` (passed).

Added `DATA_PLANE_RECORD_BLOCK` and `DATA_PLANE_RECORD_BLOCK_COMPLETE` record types to data plane protocol. Server-side: `stream_via_data_plane_resume` uses gRPC for block hash exchange then TCP data plane for block transfer - combines best of both worlds. Client-side: `handle_block_record` and `handle_block_complete_record` in data plane receiver handle seek+write for in-place block updates. Takeaway filed: small/mixed PUSH is blit's one loss to rsync on this rig — push-side per-file receive cost is the actionable gap (queue-candidate alongside w6-2b territory); rsyncd's r1 large-push 7.2 s was a one-time cold outlier (r2 1.01 s representative). rsyncd left running on skippy:8730 alongside blitd for further comparison work; both torn down at session close.

**2026-07-04 20:04:30Z** - **CODER (w3-1-memory-aware-buffer-pool, claude)**: Landed w3-1 through the codex loop (owner go: "continue" → topmost open row per the 13th handoff; its "after W2.2 settles the tuning owner" prerequisite held — owner is `engine::TransferDial`, so the spec's `for_data_plane(tuning, streams)` became `for_data_plane(chunk_bytes, streams)`, the chunk read from the dial at each site). A 5-agent audit workflow re-verified the 2026-06-11 evidence against post-REV4 HEAD before coding: exactly three formula sites survive (push client, pull_sync multistream, pull_sync resume — the daemon pull.rs copy died with the Pull RPC at ue-r2-1h); the resume site is a hand-rolled `pool_size = 4` whose pool is **inert at runtime** (resume only sends via `send_block*`, which write caller slices — `pool.acquire` is reached solely from `send_file_double_buffered`), so unifying it to the formula's 6 is behavior-neutral; the double-buffered sender holds TWO pool buffers acquired sequentially (hold-one-wait-for-second), so any memory cap admitting fewer than 2 buffers per live stream can deadlock a sender against itself; shrinking pool buffers below the session's chunk_bytes is wire-safe (file bytes travel raw under a size-carrying header — no per-chunk framing; the effective send granularity already IS the pool buffer size); and `dial.ceiling_max_streams()` is a hard 3-layer-enforced bound on live streams under resize, with ADDed streams sharing the epoch-0 pool on both elastic paths. Slice `f49f8f6`: `BufferPool::for_data_plane` in buffer.rs backed by pure `data_plane_pool_params(chunk_bytes, streams, available_memory)` — formula unchanged when memory is plentiful (pinned pure-hoist parity), budget capped at available/4 (the pool's own doc example, ignored by every call site until now), liveness floor `budget ≥ buffer_size × streams × 2` always beats the cap with buffer_size shrinking toward the shared floor instead of concurrency; elastic paths authorize `ceiling_max_streams()` up front (lazy allocation makes the ceiling authorization free until resize ADDs streams — closes both sites' "growing the pool live is a W3.1 concern" deferral without live-growth machinery); resume passes 1. **Bonus real bug fixed**: the hoisted `available_memory_bytes()` drops the old helper's `* 1024` — sysinfo 0.38 returns BYTES not KiB (verified against the vendored crate source), so available memory was over-reported 1024×, which had made BufferSizer's /10 cap vacuous forever and would have made the new /4 cap vacuous too; also `System::new()`+`refresh_memory()` replaces the process-table-walking `new_all()`, zero-report 512 MiB fallback kept. `DATA_PLANE_BUFFER_FLOOR` (64 KiB) exported and adopted at the same-semantic floor sites (session chunk clamp, receive-buffer clamp, dial inflight clamp — whose comment already said "matching the session's minimum buffer"); coincidentally-equal 64 KiB literals deliberately untouched. Comment-truth: `RECEIVE_CHUNK_SIZE`'s false "matches the send side" claim rewritten (receive is deliberately 1 MiB vs the sender's 16–64 MiB; the asymmetry is legal — no per-chunk framing); BufferPool header example now shows the constructor. Tests: +8 params-layer pins (legacy parity, floor, cap, shrink-preserving-liveness, tiny-cap liveness override, full-grid liveness/floor property sweep, zero-memory fallback, real-sysinfo smoke), mutation-verified (cap+liveness line reverted → 3 pins fail; restored → green). **2026-06-11 00:42:30Z** - **REVIEW**: Verification and acceptance of `audit-h3c-slice1-grpc-fallback-frame-contract` (commit `bf4cc82`, verdict declared by owner). Validation suite re-run at HEAD `1be16bc`: fmt/clippy/test all green (exit 0), blit-core test-function count identical at `bf4cc82` and HEAD (344) — no test drop. The review assessment surfaced four facts the finding doc didn't know, recorded here as input to the slice-2 re-scope: **(1)** the 1 MiB frame cap is load-bearing correctness, not just cadence — tonic 0.14's default 4 MiB decode limit (`DEFAULT_MAX_RECV_MESSAGE_SIZE`, no `max_decoding_message_size` override anywhere in the workspace) means pre-slice-1 gRPC-fallback transfers of files >4 MiB should fail at decode, since `tuning.rs` emits 16/32/64 MiB chunks and `pull_sync.rs:515` passed `tuning.chunk_bytes` straight into `GrpcServerStreamingSink`. Version-skew residual: a new client against an old daemon still receives uncapped frames. **(2)** The bigger H3 hole is missing client-side HTTP/2 keepalive: daemon pings clients (`main.rs:138`) but all three client channel builders (`pull.rs:239`, `push/client/mod.rs:307`, `blit-app/src/client.rs:38` — already-drifted near-duplicates) set only `connect_timeout`, so a dead daemon hangs `message().await` forever; ~3 lines of `Endpoint` keepalive config cover dead-peer/black-hole at transport level and shrink slice 2's watchdog scope to wedged-but-alive peers only. **(3)** Fallback throughput is governed by HTTP/2 flow-control windows, not frame size — hyper defaults: client 2 MiB stream / 5 MiB conn; daemon server 1 MiB conn total → hardware-independent push-fallback ceiling on high-BDP links; `http2_adaptive_window(true)` is the no-tuning fix. **(4)** `clamp_fallback_chunk_size(x.max(1MiB))` ≡ const 1 MiB — the sinks' `chunk_bytes` param is now inert and misleading; root cause is a TCP transport parameter (`chunk_bytes`) embedded in the transport-agnostic `PlannedPayloads` (planner payload composition itself is sound). Owner direction: slice 2 re-scope deferred until after a repo-wide design-coherence review (plan doc next). Sentinel cleared, `REVIEW.md` updated to verified (`[x]`).

**2026-05-14 14:00:00Z** - **FIX**: post-edc11aa review followups. Two findings: **#1 Medium (delegated_pull logs failures as ok).** `service/core.rs:291` used `ok = !cancelled`, but `handle_delegated_pull` returned `()` and converted `run_delegated_pull` failures into an error-progress message on `tx`. So a real handler failure with the client still connected logged `delegated_pull ok ... errors=N` with `N` unchanged — the operator-facing metric contradicted the actual RPC result. Fix: `handle_delegated_pull` now returns `bool` (true=success, false=failure). The phased error is still surfaced on `tx` as before; the bool is purely the success bit. Caller in `service/core.rs` consumes via `tokio::select!` into `Option<bool>` — `None` = client cancelled, `Some(true)` = handler ok, `Some(false)` = handler failed. `ok = matches!(outcome, Some(true))`; `inc_error` fires only on `Some(false)` (handler failure), not on client cancellation. New regression test `handle_delegated_pull_returns_false_on_handler_failure` drives a blank-host source locator to trip `DelegationRejected` and asserts `false` is returned — pins the return-bool contract without mocking the full pipeline. **#2 Low (release-plan inconsistency).** Top-tracker said §3.1/§3.2/§3.3 closed, but §6 commit-sequence table still labeled steps 9–11 "Not started," step 1 said D4/D5/D6 still open, step 13 still claimed tagging is blocked on "product-owner ack of P1 deferrals," and §7 heading still said D4/D5/D6 are open. All four sites rewritten to reflect 2026-05-13 reality: steps 9–11 carry closing commits (`0d76c4f`, `6e750b9`, `6e750b9`); step 1 says "all taken — D5 modified by owner"; step 13 shows tagging blocked on step 2 only; §7 heading says "all D1–D9 decided, nothing owed anymore" with the section name retained for historical reference. **Tests**: `cargo fmt --all -- --check` clean; `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean; `cargo test --workspace` all pass (+1 delegated_pull regression test).

**2026-05-14 12:00:00Z** - **FIX**: post-6e750b9 review followups against the --metrics work. Four findings: **#1 Medium (active-gauge race).** `format_completion_line` was reading `active_transfers` while the just-finished RPC's `_guard` was still in scope, so a single completed transfer logged `active=1` — misleading for an end-of-RPC summary. Fix: rename `let _guard = guard;` to `let guard = guard;` and `drop(guard);` explicitly before the `log_completion` call in all three spawn closures (push / pull / pull_sync at `service/core.rs`). Now `active=N` reflects state AFTER the just-finished RPC is removed from the gauge. **#2 Medium (missing RPC coverage).** `delegated_pull` increments `pull_ops` + the active gauge inside `run_delegated_pull` (`delegated_pull.rs:227`) but never emitted its own completion line — the field would only become visible on a later push/pull log. Same for `purge`. Fix: (a) wrapped the delegated_pull spawn closure in core.rs with a start-time capture and a `log_completion("delegated_pull", ...)` call after the cancellation `select!`; `ok = !cancelled` per the cancellation-race semantics. (b) Extracted `BlitService::purge_inner` so the trait `purge` method can wrap a single call site with start-time capture + `log_completion("purge", ...)` + `inc_error` on `Err`. Both paths now contribute to `--metrics` per-RPC summary symmetrically. **#3 Medium (rustfmt clean).** Already clean on `HEAD` (the prior `cargo fmt --all` at the tail of `6e750b9` had landed); reviewer was working off an older snapshot. No action. **#4 Low (stale scope text).** Three sites still claimed `--metrics` was dormant / scaffolding-only after the §3.1 closure: (a) `crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:82` comment block rewritten to reference `log_completion` and call out the new operator-facing summary lines; the `--metrics` `eprintln!` info line now says "per-RPC summary lines on stderr." (b) `docs/plan/RELEASE_PLAN_v2_2026-05-04.md:500` — old "No reader / dormant" analysis paragraph quoted as historical context inside a "Resolved 2026-05-13" callout, so the section reads consistently as closed without losing the audit-time reasoning. (c) `TODO.md:248` — AI telemetry line struck through with explicit `Removed from scope 2026-05-13` callout pointing at §5.4 + deletion of the doc; predictor note added to clarify perf-history collection is unaffected. **New regression test:** `completion_line_reflects_active_after_guard_drop` constructs an in-flight transfer + a finishing transfer, drops the finishing guard, and asserts `active=1` in the formatted line — pins the call-site contract that the formatter sees post-drop state. **Verified:** `cargo fmt --all -- --check` clean, `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean, `cargo test --workspace` all pass (+1 new metrics test, 9 total in `metrics::tests`).

**2026-05-05 20:30:00Z** - **FIX**: Round 45 review of commit `f83a208`. **R45-F1 (High)**: while plumbing scanned features I left a `let total_bytes = scanned_bytes` alias in `crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/orchestrator.rs:480` and the streaming summary at `:567` then read that local for `summary.total_bytes`. Net effect on the wire: `summary.total_bytes` (contracted as "bytes the pipeline wrote") was reporting scanned bytes, so any incremental skip-unchanged run with all-up-to-date files would have reported the full source size as bytes-written and overcounted throughput. Fix: removed the alias; streaming summary now reads `pipeline_outcome.bytes_written` from `SinkOutcome` directly. The verbose "Planning enumerated" line correctly references `scanned_bytes`. **R45-F2 (Low)**: planner + transfer sub-predictions were still passing `(all_headers.len(), total_bytes)` (which were aliases of scanned_* but only by accident) while the total prediction passed `(scanned_files, scanned_bytes)` explicitly. Made all three predictor calls share the explicit `(scanned_files, scanned_bytes)` feature vector so a future maintainer editing one branch can't reintroduce drift by missing another. New regression test `incremental_run_total_bytes_excludes_skipped_files` in `orchestrator::orchestrator::async_runtime_tests` runs the full local mirror pipeline twice (mirror=true forces streaming planner; skip_unchanged=true means run 2 writes 0 bytes) and asserts `summary.total_bytes == 0` on the second run. Verified the test catches the bug by reintroducing the alias — assertion fires with `total_bytes=4096, scanned_bytes=4096` matching the pre-R45 state. **Tests**: `cargo test --workspace` 407 pass / 0 fail (was 406, +1 new R45 regression test).

**2026-05-05 19:30:00Z** - **FIX**: Round 44 review of commit `da6ced2`. **R44-F1 (Medium)**: predictor train/query feature mismatch. The pre-pipeline query in `crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/orchestrator.rs` used `(all_headers.len(), total_bytes)` (scan-side workload), but `record_performance_history` recorded `summary.copied_files` for `PerformanceRecord.file_count`. On any incremental run the predictor saw "predict 1000 files" then trained on "5 files actually copied" — estimates drifted badly. Fix: added `scanned_files: usize` and `scanned_bytes: u64` to `LocalMirrorSummary` (`crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/summary.rs`) with a load-bearing rustdoc explaining the scan-vs-copy split; populated at every summary construction site (streaming pipeline, NoWork, Tiny, Huge, JournalSkip, single-file copy); `record_performance_history` now reads `summary.scanned_{files,bytes}` for the record's feature fields. The bucket-shape counters (`tar_shard_*`, `raw_bundle_*`, `large_*`) still reflect actual writes — they feed `derive_local_plan_tuning` which heuristically sizes destination buckets from past apply behavior, not scan size. Extracted `build_performance_record` from `record_performance_history` so the contract is unit-testable without polluting the global JSONL. Two new tests in `orchestrator::history::tests`: `record_uses_scanned_features_not_copied` (would have failed pre-fix on a 1000-scanned/5-copied incremental) and `bucket_counts_still_reflect_actual_writes` (regression guard against accidentally rerouting bucket counters through scan stats). **R44-F2 (Low)**: `blit profile --json` shape was unasserted. The pre-fix commit message claimed top-level `"predictor": null` for the empty-state, but actual output emits `{"copy": null, "mirror": null}` (predictor file loads even when no profile yet has training data). Picked the structured shape — strictly more informative — and pinned it in `test_utils_profile_json` (`crates/blit-cli/tests/blit_utils.rs`) with assertions covering both empty and trained states. **R44 plan note**: §2.8 of `docs/plan/RELEASE_PLAN_v2_2026-05-04.md` is correctly framed now as "predictor observability and training," not "adaptive planning behavior" — the predictor is queried, surfaced via `--verbose` and `blit profile --json`, and audit-able, but the Tiny fast-path still does not consult it for routing. **2026-05-05 18:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: §2.8 phase 2 of `docs/plan/RELEASE_PLAN_v2_2026-05-04.md` — orchestrator and `blit profile` now actually query the predictor. Three load-bearing changes: (1) `crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/orchestrator.rs` introduces a `plan_done = Instant::now()` checkpoint between the planner stage and the pipeline so `planner_duration_ms` and `transfer_duration_ms` are correctly attributed; pre-fix both fields fed `record_performance_history` got the same whole-run time, so v1 predictor training collapsed into a single regressor. (2) Just before kicking off `execute_sink_pipeline`, the orchestrator queries `predictor.predict(DurationKind::Total/Planner/Transfer, ...)` with the just-scanned `all_headers.len()` and `total_bytes`; populates `LocalMirrorSummary.predictor_estimate` (new field of type `PredictorEstimate { planner_ms, transfer_ms, total_ms, observations, fallback_depth }` in `summary.rs`). `--verbose` now emits two lines: a "Predictor estimate: ..." pre-run line and a "Predictor delta: ..." post-run line showing predicted-vs-actual percent error per phase. (3) `crates/blit-cli/src/profile.rs::run_profile` now calls `predictor.coefficients_for(mode-only, ...)` for both Copy and Mirror, surfaces the result as a coefficients block in human output (`alpha_ms_per_file`, `beta_ms_per_mb`, `gamma_ms` per planner/transfer pair) and as a `predictor.{copy,mirror}` JSON object under `--json`. **2026-05-05 18:00:00Z** - **ACTION**: §2.8 phase 1 of `docs/plan/RELEASE_PLAN_v2_2026-05-04.md` — extended the predictor data model so its predictions can actually drive decisions. Schema bumped to v2; existing `PerformancePredictor::load` already drops state on version mismatch, so the bump is transparent. New types: `DurationCoefficients` (planner + transfer coefficient pair per profile), `DurationKind { Planner, Transfer, Total }`, `Prediction { predicted_ms, observations, fallback_depth }`. New API: `predict(kind, mode, src_fs, dst_fs, fast_path, skip_unchanged, checksum, file_count, total_bytes) -> Option<Prediction>` walks a fallback chain — exact key → drop fast_path → drop dest_fs → drop src_fs → mode-only — gated at each step by `MIN_OBSERVATIONS_FOR_CONFIDENCE = 5`. `predict_planner(record)` / `predict_transfer(record)` / `predict_total(record)` are convenience wrappers around `predict(...)`. `coefficients_for(...)` returns the same `DurationCoefficients` clone that `blit profile --json` will surface in phase 2. `observe(record)` now updates BOTH coefficient sets in lockstep (single shared observation counter) so `transfer_duration_ms` becomes a load-bearing input. Removed the old `predict_ms(record) -> f64` and `predict_planner_ms(...) -> Option<(f64, u64)>` — both pre-v2 entry points returned values without confidence gating. Eight new unit tests added: `predict_below_confidence_threshold_returns_none`, `predict_above_confidence_threshold_returns_value` (verifies `fallback_depth == 0`), `predictor_learns_planner_and_transfer_independently`, `predict_total_sums_planner_and_transfer`, `fallback_chain_drops_fast_path_then_dest_then_src`, `schema_version_mismatch_resets_state_on_load`. Existing tests rewritten to use the new API. Phase 2 (orchestrator wire + verbose surface + `blit profile --json` exposure + Tiny fast-path extension when planner-dominant) lands in the next commit. **Tests**: `cargo test --workspace` 404 pass / 0 fail (was 399, +5 new predictor tests + 3 retained-with-new-API).

**2026-05-05 17:00:00Z** - **FIX**: R43 follow-up to R42-F2. The R42 commit added a comment on `MultiStreamSender::finish` claiming it routed through `drain_pipeline_error`, but the body still hand-rolled the same match arms — comment lied about the factoring. Real fix: extracted `drain_pipeline_outcome(handle: JoinHandle<...>) -> Result<SinkOutcome>` as the underlying primitive (Ok-on-clean / wrap-on-err / panic-prefix-on-join). `drain_pipeline_error` now delegates to it for the failure cases and only adds the "Ok-but-channel-closed" race-diagnostic on top. `finish()` calls `drain_pipeline_outcome(handle).await?` directly. **2026-05-05 16:00:00Z** - **FIX**: §2.7 of `docs/plan/RELEASE_PLAN_v2_2026-05-04.md` — closed `docs/plan/POST_REVIEW_FIXES.md` Round 1. **§1.1**: `let _ = file.flush().await` in `sink.rs::write_file_stream` now propagates as a `Status::internal`-style error via `with_context("flushing {dst}")?` — flush failure is a data-loss signal (user believes file is durable when it isn't). **2026-05-02 22:15:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 15 finding R15-F1 (Low) — F11's user-facing closure. The previous F11 fix added daemon ack-mismatch handling in `RemotePullClient::pull_sync`, but `transfers/endpoints.rs::ensure_remote_transfer_supported` rejected `--checksum` for ALL remote transfers before the new code could fire. F11's CLI behavior was therefore unreachable. Made the gate direction-aware: `ensure_remote_pull_supported` allows `--checksum` (the F11 ack negotiates), `ensure_remote_push_supported` keeps it rejected for push/remote-remote (no equivalent capability negotiation in the push protocol yet). New integration test `remote_checksum_negotiation.rs` spins up a daemon with `--no-server-checksums`, runs `blit copy --checksum server:/test/file.txt dest`, and asserts (a) the client refuses with a clear ack-mismatch error, (b) no file is copied via silent fallback. Companion test confirms the same command succeeds against a daemon with checksums enabled. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (188 lib + 23 daemon + 27 metrics-test bin + 2 new checksum-negotiation integration tests, all green).

**2026-05-02 21:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed F5, F11, F12, F9 from `docs/reviews/codebase_review_2026-05-01.md` — the lower-priority items from the baseline triage. **F5** (Medium): replaced inc_active/dec_active scattered around `service/core.rs` with `TransferMetrics::enter_transfer() -> ActiveGuard`, an RAII handle that decrements on Drop so panics/cancellation can't leak the gauge. Moved `inc_purge` to dispatch boundary so it counts attempts (matching push/pull semantics) instead of successes. Module doc updated with the attempts/errors/gauge contract. 5 metrics tests including panic-recovery assertion. **F11** (Medium): pull_sync receive loop now stores `ack.server_checksums_enabled` on `RemotePullReport` and bails early at the ack if the user requested `--checksum` but the daemon has checksums disabled — silent fallback to size+mtime would lie about the comparison strength the user asked for. **F12** (Low–Medium): documented `blit check` equivalence model in CLI `--help` (new `CHECK_SEMANTICS_HELP` constant, `after_long_help` on `CheckArgs`) and `CheckArgs` rustdoc. Pinned the documented behavior with 6 unit tests covering: matching-files-zero-diffs, empty-dirs-not-in-equivalence, symlinks-skipped, file-vs-dir-mismatch-on-file-side, missing-on-dest, --one-way ignores extras. **F9** (Medium): split `execute_local_mirror` into a sync wrapper + new `execute_local_mirror_async`.
