**2026-05-02 20:15:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 13 finding R13-F1 (Medium). The F2 fix protected per-file writes via `resolve_contained_path`, but the push-mirror purge path enumerates `module.path` (post-mutation by `destination_path`) before the per-entry containment check fires. If the supplied `destination_path` traversed an in-module symlink pointing outside the module root, the purge would enumerate outside the canonical root before refusing any individual delete. Two-layer fix: (1) `push/control.rs` now calls `verify_contained(&canonical_root, &new_path)` immediately after the destination_path mutation, rejecting the push at handshake; (2) `purge_extraneous_entries` calls `verify_contained` before enumeration, defense-in-depth for any future caller that bypasses the handshake check. New integration test `f2_push_destination_path_symlink_rejected` spins up a daemon, places `module/escape -> /sibling`, attempts `blit mirror src/ server:/test/escape/`, and asserts both the daemon refusal and that `/sibling`'s files were not touched. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (186 lib + 20 daemon + 3 F2 integration tests, all green).

**2026-05-02 19:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed F2 from `docs/reviews/codebase_review_2026-05-01.md` — the highest-severity remaining baseline finding. The lexical `safe_join` chokepoint catches `../`/abs/UNC/Windows-shaped wire paths but doesn't follow symlinks, so a pre-existing symlink inside a module pointing outside the root (e.g. `module/escape -> /etc`) would have any daemon read/write follow it. New `path_safety::contained_join` (and `verify_contained` for already-resolved targets) walks to the deepest existing ancestor, canonicalizes, and confirms `starts_with(canonical_module_root)`. 10 unit tests cover symlink-escape rejection (top-level, deep, parent-of-nonexistent), legit intra-module symlinks, lexical-traversal rejection, and the empty-rel single-file case. Wired into every daemon site that touches a path under a module root: `service/core.rs` (list, find, du, purge), `service/admin.rs` (delete_rel_paths_sync, stream_disk_usage, stream_find_entries), `service/pull.rs` and `service/pull_sync.rs` (pull entry-point), `service/push/data_plane.rs` (file dest + tar shard apply), `service/push/control.rs` (file_requires_upload). Added a separate `canonical_root: PathBuf` field on `ModuleConfig` because the push handler mutates `module.path` to bake in destination subpaths (rsync "copy into here" semantics) — containment must check against the never-mutated original. New integration tests in `crates/blit-cli/tests/f2_chroot_containment.rs` spin up a real daemon, place a symlink inside the module pointing outside, attempt to pull through it, assert the daemon refuses with a containment error, and verify the sensitive sibling file was not copied. Companion test confirms legit intra-module symlinks (`latest -> v1`) still work. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (186 lib + 20 daemon + integration suites, all green). F2 closes the last release-blocking security finding from the original baseline review.

**2026-05-02 18:00:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 11 finding R11-F1 (High) — completed F7 properly. The previous F7 fix bounded the *reservation* via `try_reserve_exact` but the actual `read_to_end` call would still grow the Vec past that bound if the remote source streamed extra bytes. A peer could declare `header.size = 4` and stream 1 GiB; the post-read length check would catch the discrepancy but only after the buffer had grown past the bound. Fix: extract `read_remote_entry_bounded` as a generic helper that wraps the reader with `tokio::io::AsyncReadExt::take(size + 1)` so the read itself is capped; the +1 is the over-read canary that triggers the post-read length check. Helper is `R: AsyncRead + Unpin` so tests use `std::io::Cursor` instead of a real `RemotePullClient` mock. 5 new tests in `remote_bounded_read_tests`: happy path, under-read, over-read (verifies buffer caps at size+1 even when source sends 1 MiB), defensive cap rejection, empty file. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (176 lib + 20 daemon + integration suites, all green). F7 now fully closed.

**2026-05-02 17:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed F7 + F8 from `docs/reviews/codebase_review_2026-05-01.md` (the original baseline review) in one small hardening pass. **F7** (now elevated to High in the triage): `RemoteTransferSource::prepare_payload` was doing `Vec::with_capacity(header.size as usize)` from a daemon-controlled `FileHeader.size` — the send-side mirror of R6-F1 that affects remote→remote transfers. Extracted `validate_remote_tar_shard_sizes` as a private helper that bounds both per-entry and cumulative shard sizes against `tar_safety::MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES`, uses `checked_add` for the sum, and is unit-testable without a `RemotePullClient` mock. Replaced the unbounded `Vec::with_capacity` with `try_reserve_exact`, plus an explicit length-match check after `read_to_end` so a remote source that lies about a file's size produces a hard error rather than a malformed tar. **F8**: `MAX_WIRE_TAR_SHARD_BYTES` in pipeline.rs was 1 GiB while the helper's `MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES` is 256 MiB — the wire reader accepted shards the helper would reject. Single source of truth: `MAX_WIRE_TAR_SHARD_BYTES = tar_safety::MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES as usize` (const). 5 new tests in `remote_tar_size_tests` (within bounds, at cap, per-entry above cap, cumulative above cap, u64 overflow). **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (171 lib + 20 daemon + integration suites, all green).

**2026-05-02 16:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 9 finding R9-F1 (Low). The R8-F2 fix (rejecting stream EOF without UploadComplete) was previously verified by code review only — the new framing-helper unit tests covered R8-F1 size/cap rules but not the actual EOF path through `receive_fallback_data`. To make the function unit-testable without a real gRPC server, generic-ified its signature over `tokio_stream::Stream<Item = Result<ClientPushRequest, Status>>` (tonic::Streaming already implements this trait, so production callers are unchanged) and switched the loop body from `.message()` to `.next().await.transpose()` — semantically identical. 3 new regression tests in `data_plane::tests` drive the function over `tokio_stream::iter` of synthetic message vectors: EOF after `FileManifest`, EOF after `TarShardHeader`, and EOF on an empty stream (no UploadComplete ever). All three assert the rejection now lives in the test suite, not just code review. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (166 lib + 20 daemon + integration suites, all green).

**2026-05-02 15:45:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 8 review findings R8-F1 and R8-F2 from `docs/reviews/followup_review_2026-05-02.md`. Both bugs were in the daemon's gRPC push fallback receive loop (`receive_fallback_data` in `crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs`) — the framing layer that runs *before* the shared `tar_safety` helper sees the buffer. **R8-F1** (Medium — DoS): the chunk accumulator was capped only by an 8 MiB initial reservation; the actual `Vec` grew unbounded. `archive_size == 0` skipped the overflow check entirely, and `archive_size > MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES` was bypassed at the framing layer. Reject zero archive_size when files are present, reject `archive_size > MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES` at TarShardHeader, and enforce both the declared size and the local cap on every chunk via a new `check_fallback_chunk_overflow` helper. **R8-F2** (Medium — silent partial success): stream EOF was treated as graceful end. But FileManifest and TarShardHeader remove entries from `pending` before bytes arrive, so a client could send a header, close the stream, and the final `pending.is_empty()` check would pass despite no data ever landing. Track `upload_complete_seen` and bail on EOF without UploadComplete or with `active.is_some()`. Extracted `validate_fallback_shard_archive_size` and `check_fallback_chunk_overflow` as private helpers so the rules are unit-testable without spinning up a full gRPC server. 7 new framing tests pin every boundary condition (zero size, at-cap, above cap, declared overflow, local-cap overflow, u64 overflow, within-bounds). **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (166 lib + 17 daemon + integration suites, all green).

**2026-05-02 14:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Round 7 cleanup — extracted shared `tar_safety` primitive in `blit-core/src/remote/transfer/tar_safety.rs` and migrated all three tar-shard receive sites onto it: `pull.rs::apply_pull_tar_shard` (gRPC fallback), `sink.rs::write_tar_shard_payload` (TCP data plane + local-local), `blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs::apply_tar_shard_sync` (daemon push receive). The migration closed a previously-latent High-severity bug on the daemon side: `apply_tar_shard_sync` was calling `Entry::unpack`, so an authenticated push client could ship a tar shard with a Symlink entry at a benign path pointing at `/etc/passwd` and a later push to that path would write through the symlink — same R5-F2 class as the pull side, but server-side. New regression test `apply_tar_shard_rejects_symlink_entry` proves the daemon now rejects non-regular entries up front. The shared helper also brought R6-F1 size bounds and R6-F3 mtime/permissions preservation to `sink.rs` and the daemon, where they were missing. 8 new unit tests in `tar_safety::tests`; net +8 lib tests workspace-wide (166 total). **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` all green.

**2026-05-02 13:15:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 6 review findings R6-F1 through R6-F3 from `docs/reviews/followup_review_2026-05-02.md`. **R6-F1** (Medium — DoS via per-entry size): `apply_pull_tar_shard` was preallocating with `Vec::with_capacity(header.size as usize)`, where `header.size` came from the daemon-authored `TarShardHeader.files`. A daemon could keep the shard `archive_size` under the 256 MiB cap while putting `u64::MAX` in a per-file header, forcing a huge initial allocation. Now validates `entry.size() == header.size` and `header.size <= shard.declared_size <= MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES` before any allocation, then uses `Vec::try_reserve_exact` so a still-pathological size returns `AllocError` instead of aborting. **R6-F2** (Medium — silent partial success): if the gRPC stream ended with `active_shard = Some(_)` (Header sent, no Complete), the receive loop dropped the buffered shard and returned success. Extracted the post-loop check into `ensure_no_open_shard` and made it bail with a wire protocol error — same treatment as `FileData` without a preceding `FileHeader`. **R6-F3** (Medium — metadata desync): manual tar-shard writes weren't applying `header.mtime_seconds` or `header.permissions`, so a forced-gRPC pull of many small files succeeded byte-for-byte but left destination mtimes at "now", causing the next size+mtime sync to re-transfer everything. Now applies mtime via `filetime::set_file_mtime` when `> 0` and Unix permissions when nonzero, mirroring `FsTransferSink`. 3 new unit tests in `tar_shard_safety_tests` (rejects oversized per-entry size, rejects open shard at end-of-stream, preserves mtime). **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (158 lib tests + integration suites, all green).

**2026-05-02 11:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 5 review findings R5-F1 through R5-F5 from `docs/reviews/followup_review_2026-05-02.md`. **R5-F1** (High — data-loss vector): `delete_listed_paths` used a lexical `target.starts_with(dest_root)` check that lets `dest_root.join("../victim")` pass. Routed every wire-supplied path through `path_safety::safe_join`, switched `RemotePullReport::paths_to_delete` from `Vec<PathBuf>` to `Vec<String>` so wire input never gets blessed into a path before validation, and added 4 unit tests in `delete_list_safety_tests` covering parent-traversal, absolute paths, root-self-reference, and the happy path. **R5-F2** (High — wire-controlled symlink/hardlink creation): `apply_pull_tar_shard` was calling `Entry::unpack` which honors tar's symlink/hardlink/device entry types. Rewrote to reject anything that isn't `EntryType::Regular` or `EntryType::Continuous`, validate the path through `validate_wire_path`, copy bytes manually, and verify per-entry size matches the corresponding `FileHeader.size`. Added 4 unit tests including a hand-crafted malicious tar with `../escape.txt` in its header. **R5-F3** (Medium — DoS via huge `archive_size`): `Vec::with_capacity(header.archive_size as usize)` was a daemon-controlled allocation. Added `MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES = 256 MiB` cap, modest initial reservation (capped at 1 MiB), per-chunk overflow check against `declared_size` and the local cap, and a final length check on `TarShardComplete`. **R5-F4** (Low — comment lied about validation): `filter_from_spec` claimed to validate glob patterns but only copied them into `FileFilter` for later silent dropping. Now compiles each include/exclude pattern through `globset::Glob::new` at the spec normalizer; 2 new tests pin rejection of malformed brackets. **R5-F5** (Low — DEVLOG ordering): added this header and moved newest entries to the top so review workflow doesn't depend on knowing how to find appended-at-the-bottom changes. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (152+ lib tests, all integration suites green).

**2026-05-02 09:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Step 4C — tar-shard support on the gRPC pull fallback. The push gRPC fallback runs the unified planner and emits TarShardHeader/Chunk/Complete for batched small-file workloads; the pull side previously sent files one-by-one via a hand-written loop. New `GrpcServerStreamingSink` (mirror of `GrpcFallbackSink`) in `blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs` lets the daemon's `stream_via_grpc` run `execute_sink_pipeline` with the same planner output as the TCP data plane. Proto adds three new ServerPullMessage variants (fields 13/14/15) reusing the existing TarShard message types. Client receive loop in `pull_sync` adds three match arms with an `InProgressShard` buffer and an `apply_pull_tar_shard` extractor (mirror of the daemon's push-side `apply_tar_shard_sync`). New integration test `test_pull_grpc_fallback_many_small_files` exercises 50 small files via `--force-grpc`. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (all green); `cargo test -p blit-cli --test remote_parity` (5 tests including the new one, all pass).

**2026-05-02 08:45:00Z** - **ACTION**: Step 4B — closed F10 (filter parity on pull) and F4 (mirror deletion correctness). The daemon now builds a `FileFilter` from `spec.filter` and threads it into `collect_pull_entries_with_checksums` so source enumeration honors `--exclude/--include/--min-size/--max-size/--min-age/--max-age/--files-from` exactly as a push would. After diff, a new `scope_deletions(...)` helper applies `MirrorMode` + filter scope and produces the authoritative deletion list, which the daemon ships to the client via a new `ServerPullMessage::DeleteList` variant. The CLI replaces the prior dest-tree-walking `purge_extraneous_local` with `delete_listed_paths`, which executes exactly what the daemon said (with bounded-path safety). New `--delete-scope <subset|all>` flag selects between `MirrorMode::FilteredSubset` (default — out-of-scope files preserved) and `MirrorMode::All` (every absent file purged). 6 new unit tests for scope_deletions; 2 new integration tests in `remote_pull_mirror` covering FilteredSubset preservation and `--delete-scope all` purge behavior. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (all green); `cargo test -p blit-cli --test remote_pull_mirror` (3 integration tests, all pass).

**2026-05-02 06:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed R2-F1, R4-F1, R4-F2, R4-F4 from `docs/reviews/followup_review_2026-05-02.md`. (1) DiffPlanner's `local_needs_copy` now has concrete behavior for every `ComparisonMode` (SizeOnly, IgnoreTimes, Force, Checksum, SizeMtime/Unspecified) instead of silently falling through to size+mtime; 10 new per-mode tests. (2) Daemon PullSync handler routes through `NormalizedTransferOperation::from_spec` so spec_version mismatch and unknown enum values become hard `invalid_argument` errors at the wire boundary. (3) `ignore_existing` is now an orthogonal `bool` field on `TransferOperationSpec` (proto field 10; old enum value 5 reserved); `compare_mode = Force && ignore_existing` is rejected at the spec normalizer; CLI adds `conflicts_with = "force"` on `--ignore-existing`; orchestrator threads the flag through `LocalMirrorOptions → LocalDiffInputs` so local-local copies enforce it through the same planner as remote paths. (4) Refreshed stale proto comments referring to removed `PullSyncHeader` and the old "supports_filter_spec fallback" plan. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (all green, 144+ core tests).

**2026-05-02 04:15:00Z** - **STEP 4A (PullSync wire migration to TransferOperationSpec)**: With no backwards-compat constraint into the next release, replaced the bool-soup `PullSyncHeader` (5 booleans for comparison mode + separate fields for resume/mirror/force_grpc) with the unified `TransferOperationSpec` defined in step 2. `ClientPullMessage::Header` is now `ClientPullMessage::Spec`. `PullSyncHeader` deleted from the proto entirely. Daemon parses the spec and translates its `ComparisonMode` enum onto the existing internal `CompareMode` via a new `compare_mode_to_internal` helper that also splits out `IgnoreExisting` as the orthogonal axis it actually is. Client (`RemotePullClient::pull_sync`) constructs the spec from CLI args, advertising full `PeerCapabilities` (resume, tar shards, data plane TCP, filter spec — all true), and defaulting `mirror_mode` to `MirrorMode::FilteredSubset` rather than the old "any-mirror-mode-true" boolean. Filter not yet honored on the daemon — that's step 4B. **The bool-soup → typed-enum win is real**: nonsensical combinations like `size_only=true && checksum=true && ignore_times=true` are no longer constructible. **Tests**: 214 pass (unchanged) — pure wire-shape migration, behavior preserved end-to-end.

**2026-05-02 03:30:00Z** - **STEP 3b (push client routes through diff_planner)**: Smaller than the orchestrator migration in step 3a because push's actual diff lives on the *daemon* side — the client sends its source manifest, the daemon returns a NeedList, and the client filters its headers to that intersection before planning. There's no client-side comparison stage to consolidate. What changed: added `plan_push_payloads(headers, source_root, plan_options)` to `diff_planner` as the unified entry point for push planning (a thin wrapper over `plan_transfer_payloads` that adds a `Context` for error messages); push client's import now goes through `diff_planner` so future readers find the planning entry point in the unified module rather than reaching into `payload.rs`. Documented inline that push's diff is daemon-driven and that step 5 (remote→remote re-evaluation) might let push share daemon-side diff machinery with pull. **Tests**: 214 pass (unchanged; this is a re-export + import rename, not a behavior change).

**2026-05-02 03:00:00Z** - **F1 follow-up (R1 fixes)**: Acted on `docs/reviews/followup_review_2026-05-02.md` round 1. **R1-F1** (Medium, real bug): `validate_wire_path` accepted single-leading-backslash forms like `\Windows\System32` on Unix because `Path::components` treats backslash as a normal character there. Extended `looks_like_windows_absolute` to flag any input starting with `\`. Tests added for `\foo`, `\foo\bar`, bare `\`. **R1-F3** (Low): wire path `"."` previously normalized to empty, getting the same single-file treatment as the legitimate empty-path case. `validate_wire_path` now rejects non-empty inputs that produce zero normal components (`"."`, `"./"`, `"./."`) — those are directory hints, not file paths. Fallout: the daemon's `resolve_relative_path` (used for list/find/du request paths where `.` legitimately means "module root") needed to disambiguate between request-path and file-path contexts. Added a request-path-context fold that maps `""`, `"."`, `"./"` etc. to `PathBuf::from(".")` before invoking strict validation; file-path callers (`resolve_manifest_relative_path`, sink writes) keep using the strict validator directly. **R1-F2** (Medium): `safe_join` is lexical only — `dest_root/symlink/file` lexically passes even when `symlink` escapes the root. Reviewer correctly identified this as F2 (chroot/canonical-containment) territory, not an F1 fix. Documented the lexical-only contract prominently in `path_safety.rs` module doc with an explicit pointer to F2 for canonical-parent containment. Updated `TODO.md` F2 entry to call out the symlink-traversal concern. **Tests**: 214 pass (was 213) — net +1 from R1-F1 leading-backslash test minus zero from R1-F3 (the existing `just_dot_normalizes_to_empty` test was rewritten as `just_dot_rejected` covering three inputs in one test).

**2026-05-02 02:30:00Z** - **STEP 3a (DiffPlanner extraction, orchestrator migration)**: New `blit-core::remote::transfer::diff_planner` module consolidates the diff + payload-planning stage. Public API: `plan_local_mirror(headers, LocalDiffInputs) -> PlannedPayloads` is the single entry point the orchestrator's local-mirror path now calls; under the hood it composes `filter_unchanged` (the comparison-filter stage previously named `filter_headers_for_copy` and inlined in `orchestrator.rs`) with the existing `plan_transfer_payloads`. Translates the proto `ComparisonMode` enum onto the `Option<ChecksumType>` that the existing comparison primitives consume — `Checksum` enables Blake3, all other variants (`Unspecified`, `SizeMtime`, `SizeOnly`, `IgnoreTimes`, `IgnoreExisting`, `Force`) currently fall back to size+mtime. The non-`SizeMtime` variants are accepted at the API surface so callers can pass them through; their proper behavior arrives with step 4 (pull_sync.rs migration brings the comparison strategies that today live as `PullSyncHeader` bools). Orchestrator's local-mirror path migrated: the previous inline scan → spawn_blocking(filter_headers_for_copy) → plan_transfer_payloads sequence is now scan → spawn_blocking(plan_local_mirror) — same effect, single chokepoint, smaller call site. Dead `filter_headers_for_copy` removed. `ChecksumType` gained `PartialEq + Eq` so the diff_planner unit tests can assert mappings. **Push and pull origin paths NOT yet migrated** — those land in step 3b and step 4 respectively. **Tests**: 213 pass (+4 new diff_planner unit tests covering the ComparisonMode→ChecksumType mapping for every variant, and the filter_unchanged identity-vs-modified behavior), 0 failures. Behavior preservation verified by the unchanged orchestrator integration tests (admin verbs, remote_remote, remote_pull_mirror, remote_resume, remote_tcp_fallback all still pass).

**2026-05-02 01:45:00Z** - **STEP 2 (operation spec contract)**: Added the canonical `TransferOperationSpec` message to `proto/blit.proto` along with `FilterSpec`, `ComparisonMode` enum, `MirrorMode` enum, `ResumeSettings`, `PeerCapabilities`. Per `docs/plan/PIPELINE_UNIFICATION.md` step 2: contract only, no behavior change yet. PushHeader and PullSyncHeader stay as the today-active control messages until the DiffPlanner extraction (step 3) and pull_sync.rs refactor (step 4) port to the new spec. Notable design choices: (1) `ComparisonMode` is an enum rather than the bool soup currently in PullSyncHeader (`size_only`, `ignore_times`, `ignore_existing`, `force`, `checksum` — five booleans that admit nonsensical combinations), (2) `MirrorMode` enum makes F4's filtered-mirror-delete-scope question explicit at the wire boundary (`OFF`, `FILTERED_SUBSET`, `ALL`), (3) `optional` proto3 scalars on `FilterSpec` size/age fields so callers can distinguish "not set" from "set to 0", (4) `PeerCapabilities` is additive — new capabilities default to `false` so a missing field on an old peer reads as "not supported." Re-export module `blit-core::remote::transfer::operation_spec` so callers don't reach into the generated `blit.v2` namespace directly. **Verification**: `cargo check --workspace` clean; `cargo test --workspace` 209 pass (unchanged); generated bindings include all six new types in the build artifact.

**2026-05-02 01:15:00Z** - **F1 (path safety)**: Centralized receive-side path validation in `blit-core/src/path_safety.rs`. Two helpers: `validate_wire_path(s) -> PathBuf` (pure validation, normalized form) and `safe_join(root, s) -> PathBuf` (validate + join, with empty input returning root unchanged for the single-file destination case). Rejects: `..` components (not just substrings — the previous tar-shard `rel.contains("..")` check was too weak and also rejected legitimate filenames containing literal `..`), absolute paths, Windows drive prefixes (`C:\…`), UNC and DOS device paths (`\\?\…`, `\\server\share\…`), root components, embedded NUL bytes. Migrated `pull.rs::sanitize_relative_path` and daemon `service/util.rs::resolve_relative_path` / `resolve_manifest_relative_path` to thin wrappers that delegate to the shared module — single chokepoint, no drift between sanitizers. Applied at all five receive-side sites the review identified: `sink.rs:218` (streamed file write), `sink.rs:404` + `:426` (tar shard entry validation + per-entry join), `sink.rs:462` (resume block write), `sink.rs:498` (block completion), and the gRPC fallback block-hash path in `pull.rs:532`. Wire-boundary defense in depth: `pipeline.rs::read_file_header` and per-entry path read in `read_tar_shard` validate at the moment paths arrive off the socket, so unsafe headers never enter the FileHeader stream. **Tests**: 209 passed (was 185 baseline) — 16 new `path_safety::tests` covering the validator surface (`..`, absolute Unix, Windows drive, UNC, NUL, valid `..`-containing filenames, deep paths, Unicode, trailing slash, just-dot), 8 new sink-level integration tests confirming `FsTransferSink::write_file_stream` rejects malicious wire paths before any filesystem write and that the legitimate single-file empty-path case still works. **Verification**: `cargo check --workspace` clean; `cargo test --workspace` 0 failures.

**2026-05-02 00:30:00Z** - **PLAN**: Architecture clarification in response to GPT-5.5's review of the universal-filter / blit check / daemon-metrics work and follow-up discussion. The review's findings (esp. F1 path safety, F10 filter parity overstatement, F11 pull checksum capability) revealed the deeper architectural shape: a transfer has three roles (initiator / origin / target) and `pull_sync.rs` is the only origin path that doesn't run the unified pipeline. The corrected model is documented in `docs/plan/PIPELINE_UNIFICATION.md`: the same pipeline (`TransferSource → DiffPlanner → execute_sink_pipeline_streaming → TransferSink`) runs on whichever side holds the data, regardless of where the CLI was invoked. The unified stage is `DiffPlanner`, not `FilteredSource` — `FilteredSource` is one input among filter rules, destination manifest, comparison mode, and capabilities. The wire contract is a normalized `TransferOperationSpec`, not a flag bag. Updated `TODO.md` with the 5-step priority sequence: F1 path safety first (independent prereq), then `TransferOperationSpec` data shape, then `DiffPlanner` extraction from `pull_sync.rs`, then `pull_sync.rs` refactor onto the unified pipeline, then re-evaluate remote→remote (currently CLI-mediated relay; should become daemon-A → daemon-B direct).

**2026-05-01 23:43:57Z** - **REVIEW**: Completed a repo-level codebase review and saved it to `docs/reviews/codebase_review_2026-05-01.md`. Highest-priority findings: receive-side path sanitization is incomplete across streamed files, tar shards, and resume block records; daemon `use_chroot` is documented/configured but not enforced; filtered mirror delete semantics need an explicit product decision; metrics lifecycle and endpoint behavior need hardening. Added a short `TODO.md` follow-up section and marked Phase 4 as in progress with the review artifact linked. **Verification**: `cargo check --workspace` passed; `cargo test --workspace` passed with 185 tests after rerunning outside the sandbox to allow local test port binding.

**2026-04-24 03:15:00Z** - **FIX**: Fixed single-file remote push crash — `blit copy FILE server:/mod/` previously died with "opening FILE/ during payload planning: Not a directory". Root cause was two-sided: on the client, `filter_readable_headers` and `build_tar_shard` computed `source_root.join(&rel)` where `rel=""` for single-file sources, which on Unix preserves a trailing `/` and makes `File::open` reject with ENOTDIR. On the daemon, `resolve_relative_path` folded empty paths to `"."` (which broke `module.path.join("")` = wanted single file, but got `module.path/.`), and the subsequent `module.path.join(empty_rel)` added another trailing `/`. Fix applies the `rel.is_empty() → use root directly` pattern in three places on the client side (matching `FsTransferSource::open_file`'s existing handling), and adds two new helpers on the daemon side: `resolve_manifest_relative_path` preserves empty as empty for per-file manifest entries, and `resolve_dest_path(base, rel)` handles the empty-rel join case. Swapped all four push-side `resolve_relative_path` callers and three `module.path.join` sites. Regression tests in `crates/blit-cli/tests/remote_push_single_file.rs` pin both the container-dir (`blit copy FILE server:/mod/`) and rename (`blit copy FILE server:/mod/new.txt`) cases. Annotated all four `docs/bugs/*.md` files with their resolution status. **Tests**: 173 passed (+2 remote push single-file), clippy clean.

# 10GbE session evidence (2026-07-04, MTU 9000 both ends)
iperf3 baseline: fwd 9.88 Gbit/s (1 stream) / 9.91 (4 streams); rev 9.91
TCP push 1GiB: 934ms wall, first payload 14.5ms
TCP pull 1GiB (clean): 887ms = 9.7 Gbit/s; client stream line: 9.78 Gbps
gRPC push 1GiB (clean): 1054ms = 8.2 Gbit/s; first payload 1.01s (design-4 full-manifest gate)
Reverse (skippy client): push 7.25 Gbps data-plane / first payload 3.9ms; pull 881ms = 9.75 Gbit/s

- `docs/plan/SMALL_FILE_CEILING.md:29` — **Medium** — The plan cites gitignored logs/daemon logs as evidence for ceiling arithmetic, but the durable in-repo DEVLOG digest only records the benchmark results. Claims like “~150 µs/file proven single-pipe,” “≪ 200 ms,” and the exact one-stream/~215 µs diagnosis are not preserved in the digest, so the measured basis is not reviewable from repo records alone.

- `docs/plan/SMALL_FILE_CEILING.md:84` — **Medium** — Acceptance requires rsync-over-ssh, rclone best config, and `cp -a` tripwires, but `sf-1` only commits an `RSYNC_COMPARE=1`/rsyncd harness. The acceptance matrix is broader than the planned observable harness.

- `docs/plan/SMALL_FILE_CEILING.md:135` — **Medium** — `sf-3` combines profiling plus unspecified “cheapest cuts” across daemon receive and client pull write paths. That is not sized as one review-loop pass and has no concrete testable end state beyond a vague per-file-cost proxy.

- `docs/plan/SMALL_FILE_CEILING.md:145` — **High** — `sf-6` gates owner review before code, but does not require the REV4 wire-compat deliverables: named fields/capabilities, old/new peer behavior, and mixed-version tests before behavior depends on the tar-shard lane. This leaves a RELIABLE/wire-compat invariant gap.

- `docs/plan/SMALL_FILE_CEILING.md:87` — **Low** — “currently-winning cells” reintroduces competitor-relative language into a baseline/regression criterion. The plan should describe these as baseline or already-ceiling-bound cells, keeping competitors strictly as tripwires.
